+    /**
+     * Grab a transform between two Coordinate Reference Systems. This m=

+     * <code>{@linkplain #transform(CoordinateReferenceSystem, Coordinat=

+     * transform}(sourceCRS, targetCRS)</code>, except that it can optio=

+     * <cite>lenient datum shift</cite>. If the {@code lenient} argument=

+     * then this method will not throw a "<cite>Bursa-Wolf parameters re=

+     * exception during datum shifts if the Bursa-Wolf paramaters are no=

+     * Instead it will assume a no datum shift.
+     *=20

+     * @param  targetCRS The target CRS.

+     * @return The math transform from {@code sourceCRS} to {@code targe=

+    public static MathTransform findMathTransform(final CoordinateRefere=

+                                                  final CoordinateRefere=

+            throws FactoryException
+    {

NIENT : null);

+    /**
+     * Transforms an envelope. The transformation is only approximative.=
 Note that the returned
+     * envelope may not have the same number of dimensions than the orig=
inal envelope.
+     *
+     * @param  transform The transform to use.
+     * @param  envelope Envelope to transform, or {@code null}. This env=
elope will not be modified.
+     * @return The transformed envelope, or {@code null} if {@code envel=
ope} was null.
+     * @throws TransformException if a transform failed.
+     *
+     * @since 2.4
+     */
+    public static GeneralEnvelope transform(final MathTransform transfor=
m, final Envelope envelope)
+            throws TransformException
+    {
+        if (envelope =3D=3D null) {
+            return null;
+        }
+        if (transform.isIdentity()) {
+            /*
+             * Slight optimisation: Just copy the envelope. Note that we=
 need to set the CRS
+             * to null because we don't know what the target CRS was sup=
posed to be. Even if
+             * an identity transform often imply that the target CRS is =
the same one than the
+             * source CRS, it is not always the case. The metadata may b=
e differents, or the
+             * transform may be a datum shift without Bursa-Wolf paramet=
ers, etc.
+             */
+            final GeneralEnvelope e =3D new GeneralEnvelope(envelope);
+            e.setCoordinateReferenceSystem(null);
+            return e;
+        }
+        final int sourceDim =3D transform.getSourceDimensions();
+        final int targetDim =3D transform.getTargetDimensions();
+        if (envelope.getDimension() !=3D sourceDim) {
+            throw new MismatchedDimensionException(Errors.format(
+                      ErrorKeys.MISMATCHED_DIMENSION_$2,
+                      new Integer(sourceDim), new Integer(envelope.getDi=
mension())));
+        }
+        int          coordinateNumber =3D 0;
+        GeneralEnvelope   transformed =3D null;
+        final GeneralDirectPosition sourcePt =3D new GeneralDirectPositi=
on(sourceDim);
+        final GeneralDirectPosition targetPt =3D new GeneralDirectPositi=
on(targetDim);
+        for (int i=3DsourceDim; --i>=3D0;) {
+            sourcePt.setOrdinate(i, envelope.getMinimum(i));
+        }
+  loop: while (true) {
+            // Transform a point and add the transformed point to the de=
stination envelope.
+            if (targetPt !=3D transform.transform(sourcePt, targetPt)) {
+                throw new UnsupportedImplementationException(transform.g=
etClass());
+            }
+            if (transformed !=3D null) {
+                transformed.add(targetPt);
+            } else {
+                transformed =3D new GeneralEnvelope(targetPt, targetPt);
+            }
+            // Get the next point's coordinate.   The 'coordinateNumber'=
 variable should
+            // be seen as a number in base 3 where the number of digits =
is equals to the
+            // number of dimensions. For example, a 4-D space would have=
 numbers ranging
+            // from "0000" to "2222". The digits are then translated int=
o minimal, central
+            // or maximal ordinates.
+            int n =3D ++coordinateNumber;
+            for (int i=3DsourceDim; --i>=3D0;) {
+                switch (n % 3) {
+                    case 0:  sourcePt.setOrdinate(i, envelope.getMinimum=
(i)); n/=3D3; break;
+                    case 1:  sourcePt.setOrdinate(i, envelope.getCenter =
(i)); continue loop;
+                    case 2:  sourcePt.setOrdinate(i, envelope.getMaximum=
(i)); continue loop;
+                    default: throw new AssertionError(n); // Should neve=
r happen
+                }
+            }
+            break;
+        }
+        return transformed;
+    }
+   =20
+    /**
+     * Transforms a rectangular envelope. The transformation is only app=
roximative.
+     * Invoking this method is equivalent to invoking the following:
+     * <p>
+     * <pre>transform(transform, new GeneralEnvelope(source)).toRectangl=
e2D()</pre>
+     *
+     * @param  transform The transform to use. Source and target dimensi=
on must be 2.
+     * @param  source The rectangle to transform (may be {@code null}).
+     * @param  dest The destination rectangle (may be {@code source}).
+     *         If {@code null}, a new rectangle will be created and retu=
rned.
+     * @return {@code dest}, or a new rectangle if {@code dest} was non-=
null
+     *         and {@code source} was null.
+     * @throws TransformException if a transform failed.
+     *
+     * @todo Move this method as a static method in {@link org.geotools.=
referencing.CRS}.
+     */
+    public static Rectangle2D transform(final MathTransform2D transform,
+                                        final Rectangle2D     source,
+                                        final Rectangle2D     dest)
+            throws TransformException
+    {
+        if (source =3D=3D null) {
+            return null;
+        }
+        double xmin =3D Double.POSITIVE_INFINITY;
+        double ymin =3D Double.POSITIVE_INFINITY;
+        double xmax =3D Double.NEGATIVE_INFINITY;
+        double ymax =3D Double.NEGATIVE_INFINITY;
+        final Point2D.Double point =3D new Point2D.Double();
+        for (int i=3D0; i<8; i++) {
+            /*
+             *   (0)----(5)----(1)
+             *    |             |
+             *   (4)           (7)
+             *    |             |
+             *   (2)----(6)----(3)
+             */
+            point.x =3D (i&1)=3D=3D0 ? source.getMinX() : source.getMaxX=
();
+            point.y =3D (i&2)=3D=3D0 ? source.getMinY() : source.getMaxY=
();
+            switch (i) {
+                case 5: // fallthrough
+                case 6: point.x=3Dsource.getCenterX(); break;
+                case 7: // fallthrough
+                case 4: point.y=3Dsource.getCenterY(); break;
+            }
+            transform.transform(point, point);
+            if (point.x < xmin) xmin =3D point.x;
+            if (point.x > xmax) xmax =3D point.x;
+            if (point.y < ymin) ymin =3D point.y;
+            if (point.y > ymax) ymax =3D point.y;
+        }
+        if (dest !=3D null) {
+            dest.setRect(xmin, ymin, xmax-xmin, ymax-ymin);
+            return dest;
+        }
+        return XRectangle2D.createFromExtremums(xmin, ymin, xmax, ymax);
+    }

Log:
Extracted as much constants as possible out of the loops in Krovak projec=
tion. Also leveraged existing fields like 'centralMeridian' and edited th=
e parameter descriptors according the description found on http://www.remotesens=
ing.org. The new formulas may seem quite different than the previous ones=
, but actually they are really the same; I applied only algebraic operati=
ons that are mathematically identical. In practice (due to rounding error=
), only the two last digits sometime appear different in the tests I did.

+     * Compares the specified object with this map projection for equali=

+        if (object =3D=3D this) {
+            // Slight optimization
+            return true;
+        }

esri as plugin/epsg-extension for making room to non-ESRI extension. Note=

ard architectural design pattern designed to cleanly separate the data mo=
del from the logic used to create and modify that model. In general, this=
 architecture does not split the view and controller components in quite =
as distinctive a manner. However, the Geotools library does not provide a=

-    <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-geometry">
-      <title>The Geometric Model</title>
-
-      <para>
-        This model provides the infrastructure for defining vector based=
 geometric figures. The model is based on the idea of coordinates and of =
aggregates of these coordinates into points, lines, polygons, multipoints=
, multilines, or multipolygons. The geometric model also includes operato=
rs to perform standard computational geometry operations on the aggregate=
s. In versions up to Geotools 2.2, the Geotools library depends on the Ja=
va Topology Suite (JTS) library and is therefore limited to working in tw=
o dimensions.
-      </para>

-    </sect4>

-      <title>The Geopositioning Model</title>
-
-      <para>
-        This model provides the infrastructure for geopositioning and fo=
r common operations on geo-referenced data such as transformations and re=
-projections. This model provides ways to define Coordinate Reference Sys=
tems (CRS) and the EPSG plugins provide a standard source for the commonl=
y defined geodetic datums and CRS. The model further provide access to fu=
ndamental units and parameter structures.
-      </para>
-
-    </sect4>

-    <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-feature">
-      <title>The Feature Model</title>
-
-      <para>
-        Features are the fundamental unit of geospatial data in the term=
inology used by Geotools. Features may describe a real world entities or =
theoretical constructs. Conceptually, Features contain an identifier, a b=
unch of attributes in a java array, and a schema defining the attributes =
and the layout of these attributes within the attribute array. The attrib=
utes will include the geospatial definition of the feature, any temporal =
definition of the entity, and any other attributes of the feature. The st=
andard method to obtain feature contents is through the creation of 'quer=
ies', combinations of filters and expressions; these are described below.
-      </para>
-
-    </sect4>
-
-    <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-data">
-      <title>The Data Access and Storage Model</title>
-
-      <para>
-        This model provides methods for creating, manipulating, and stor=
ing data. The model provides an approach to storing data from different s=
ources in a single catalog structure. The model facilitates the interacti=
on with data in vector or raster formats contained on the local file syst=
em, in a database or from a network server. The plugin module provides a =
number of plugins to access common data formats such as GML files, Shapef=
ile format files, GeoTiff images, Geospatial databases, Web Mapping Serve=
rs and Web Feature Servers.
-      </para>
-
-    </sect4>

-    <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-query">

-
-      <para>
-        This model provides a standard way to discover and obtain the co=
ntents of geospatial data from the data sources and from known features. =
The query model involves the creation of Filters to sub-select the data c=
ontents and expressions to extract only the relevant attributes from the =
features of interest.
-      </para>

-<sect1 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-api">
-  <title>API</title>

-  <para>
-    Developers can use several programming interfaces through which to a=
ccess=20
-    the functionality of &geot;. Obviously, since the code is openly dis=
tributed  =20
-    and freely accessible users can develop their applications in any wa=
y they=20
-    choose. However, there are several defined series of interfaces whic=
h have
-    been created to allow users to develop applications which can be eas=
ily=20
-    updated as newer versions of &geot; are released in the future.
-  </para>
- =20
-  <para>
-    Ideally, and hopefully in the not to distant future, &geot; users wi=
ll be=20
-    able to use only a single method from Geotools and code their entire=
=20
-    application against the GeoAPI interfaces. These interfaces are desi=
gned to=20
-    follow as closely as possible the fundamental standards defined by t=
he ISO=20
-    and the OGC. Applications created in this way should be completely p=
ortable=20
-    between independent implementations of the standards.=20
-  </para>
- =20
-  <para>
-    Unfortunately the GeoAPI specifications are a work in progress so de=
velopers
-    must currently mix the use of GeoAPI interfaces, internal &geot; int=
erfaces,=20
-    interfaces defined in third party libraries and classes from &geot; =
and other=20
-    libraries. This situation is unfortunate but a consequence of the in=
complete=20
-    nature of each of these projects.
-  </para>
- =20
-  <para>
-    The best practice, for an application using the &geot; library, invo=
lves using=20
-    the GeoAPI interfaces as extensively as possible, using the internal=
 &geot;=20
-    interfaces where avaiable and then, only if none of these provide th=
e needed=20
-    functionality, using interfaces defined by third parties or using &g=
eot;=20
-    classes directly. Following such a practice will lead to the least a=
mount of=20
-    work when upgrading an application in the future to newer versions o=
f GeoAPI=20
-    and &geot;.
-  </para>

any=20
-      project can implement the fundamental geospatial standards defined=
 by the
-      ISO and the OGC.=20
-    </para>
-   =20
-    <para>
-      The &geot; library can be considered simply one implementation of =
the GeoAPI
-      interfaces. &geot; is both a proof-of-concept implementation and a=
 freely
-      distributable complement to the GeoAPI interfaces. Indeed, GeoAPI =
grew out
-      of the &geot; project because of the need for a clean separation b=
etween the
-      interfaces metting the geospatial standards and the particular imp=
lementation=20
-      provided by the project. Currently, interfaces are generally first=
 defined=20
-      as internal &geot; interfaces and gradually migrate to GeoAPI as t=
hese=20
-      interfaces prove sufficiently mature.
-    </para>

 easy=20

+    This chapter introduces the design of the &geot; library. The &geot;=
 code=20
+    library is built in modular components assembled into layers with sp=
ecific=20
+    functionality. An application using &geot; can assemble only the com=
ponents=20
+    it needs.=20

+  <sect1 id=3D"sect-design-archi">
+    <title>Architectural Design</title>
+   =20
+    <para>
+      The &geot; library runs inside a java virtual machine on one of se=
veral=20
+      operating systems. The library necessarily depends on a number of =
third=20
+      party libraries and can optionally use other libraries for specifi=
c=20
+      functionality.

+    <sect2 id=3D"sect-design-archi-runenv">
+      <title>Runtime Environment</title>
+     =20
+      <para>
+       The environment on which the Geotools library runs is shown in <x=
ref
+        linkend=3D"fig-geotools-environment" />.
+        <figure id=3D"fig-geotools-environment">
+          <title>The Geotools Environment.</title>
+          <screenshot>
+            <mediaobject>
+              <imageobject>
+                <imagedata fileref=3D"figures/geotools-environment.png"=20
+                    format=3D"PNG" />
+              </imageobject>
+              <textobject>
+                <phrase>
+                  An image of the components on which the Geotools libra=
ry runs.
+                </phrase>
+              </textobject>
+        	     <caption>
+            	  <para>
+            	    &geot; is written in Java and therefore runs inside a J=
ava Virtual=20
+                  machine (VM). The Java VM generally runs through the P=
OSIX layer=20
+                  on the hardware. The library requires two of the stand=
ard Java=20
+                  extension libraries, Java Advanced Imaging and Java Im=
age I/O. =20
+                  &geot; uses the GeoAPI project to define a standard AP=
I, the JTS=20
+                  project for robust geometric convolutions, and the def=
initions=20
+                  for scientific units provided by JSR-108 or more recen=
tly by the
+                  JScience project. There are also several external libr=
aries and=20
+                  code plugins which can be connected to &geot;.
+            	  </para>
+            	</caption>
+            </mediaobject>
+          </screenshot>
+        </figure>
+      </para>

+    </sect2>

+    <sect2 id=3D"sect-design-archi-subsys">
+      <title>Library Subsystems</title>
+
+      <para>
+         The Geotools library is split into several, essentially separat=
e components. This component architecture makes it easy to use only part =
of the library, provides a clean separation to extend Geotools with new f=
unctionality, and provides a simple way to replace the default implementa=
tion of any particular component with another implementation.
+      </para>
+
+      <para>
+       The architecture of the Geotools library runs is sketched in <xre=
f
+        linkend=3D"fig-geotools-subsystems" /> .
+        <figure id=3D"fig-geotools-subsystems">
+          <title>The General Geotools Subsystems.</title>
+          <screenshot>
+            <mediaobject>
+            <imageobject>
+              <imagedata fileref=3D"figures/geotools-subsystems.png"=20
+                  format=3D"PNG" />
+            </imageobject>
+            <textobject>
+              <phrase>
+                An image of the internal architecture of the Geotools li=
brary.
+              </phrase>
+            </textobject>
+    	<caption>
+    	  <para>
+    	    The &geot; architecture is comprised of several data subsystems=
 and a=20
+                display subsystem.
+    	  </para>
+    	</caption>
+            </mediaobject>
+          </screenshot>
+        </figure>
+      </para>
+
+      <para>
+        &geot; is comprised of several components each with various subs=
ytems. The=20
+        main library is split between the View component and the Data Mo=
del component=20
+        following the standard model/view/controller computer code patte=
rn.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        The Data Model component consists of the geometric subsystem, th=
e=20
+        geopositioning=20
+        subsystem, and the feature subsystem, which jointly provide the =
core data=20
+        model for geospatial entities. The positioning subsystem uses on=
e or more=20
+        authorities, most notably the EPSG database. &geot; also uses a =
Data access=20
+        and storage subsystem, with plugins for many common data formats=
. A Query=20
+        subsystem provides a rich facility for data selection and manipu=
lation.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        The View component consists of the display substem which provide=
s a way=20
+        to style and render features selected through a query.
+      </para>
+
+    <!-- TODO: add the ext/ and spike/ dirs -->
+
+      <para>
+    The Geotools library is split between the Main module and the Plugin=
 modules. The Main module provides the core libraries and the plugins pro=
vide specific functionality. There are several plugins that provide acces=
s to different format versions of the European Petroleum Survey Group (EP=
SG) data base of known coordinate geo-referencing systems. Similarly, the=
re are multiple plugins which provide access to common geospatial data fo=
rmats such as imagery and vector formats either on the local disk, in dat=
abases, or on the internet.
+      </para>
+
+      <para>
+    The Main module itself is split into two components, the data model =
component and the data view component. These two components are two of th=
e three components in a standard Model-View-Controller split used for mos=
t modern GUI application. The Model-View-Controller architecture is a sta=
ndard architectural design pattern designed to cleanly separate the data =
model from the logic used to create and modify that model. In general, th=
is architecture does not split the view and controller components in quit=
e as distinctive a manner. However, the Geotools library does not provide=
 any controller logic so the library is cleanly split into a Model-View d=
ivision.
+      </para>
+
+
+      <sect3 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-dataComponen=
t">
+      <title>The Data Component</title>
+
+      <para>
+        The &geot; library follows the standard split between the model,=
 view,=20
+        and controller components. The data component consists of the en=
tities=20
+        which describe the real world entities within the computational =
system.
+      </para>
+
+      <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-geometry">
+        <title>The Geometric Model</title>
+
+        <para>
+          This model provides the infrastructure for defining vector bas=
ed geometric figures. The model is based on the idea of coordinates and o=
f aggregates of these coordinates into points, lines, polygons, multipoin=
ts, multilines, or multipolygons. The geometric model also includes opera=
tors to perform standard computational geometry operations on the aggrega=
tes. In versions up to Geotools 2.2, the Geotools library depends on the =
Java Topology Suite (JTS) library and is therefore limited to working in =
two dimensions.
+        </para>
+
+      </sect4>
+
+      <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-geopositioni=
ng">
+        <title>The Geopositioning Model</title>
+
+        <para>
+          This model provides the infrastructure for geopositioning and =
for common operations on geo-referenced data such as transformations and =
re-projections. This model provides ways to define Coordinate Reference S=
ystems (CRS) and the EPSG plugins provide a standard source for the commo=
nly defined geodetic datums and CRS. The model further provide access to =
fundamental units and parameter structures.
+        </para>
+
+      </sect4>
+
+      <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-feature">
+        <title>The Feature Model</title>
+
+        <para>
+          Features are the fundamental unit of geospatial data in the te=
rminology used by Geotools. Features may describe a real world entities o=
r theoretical constructs. Conceptually, Features contain an identifier, a=
 bunch of attributes in a java array, and a schema defining the attribute=
s and the layout of these attributes within the attribute array. The attr=
ibutes will include the geospatial definition of the feature, any tempora=
l definition of the entity, and any other attributes of the feature. The =
standard method to obtain feature contents is through the creation of 'qu=
eries', combinations of filters and expressions; these are described belo=
w.
+        </para>
+
+      </sect4>
+
+      <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-data">
+        <title>The Data Access and Storage Model</title>
+
+        <para>
+          This model provides methods for creating, manipulating, and st=
oring data. The model provides an approach to storing data from different=
 sources in a single catalog structure. The model facilitates the interac=
tion with data in vector or raster formats contained on the local file sy=
stem, in a database or from a network server. The plugin module provides =
a number of plugins to access common data formats such as GML files, Shap=
efile format files, GeoTiff images, Geospatial databases, Web Mapping Ser=
vers and Web Feature Servers.
+        </para>
+
+      </sect4>
+
+      <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-query">
+        <title>The Query Model</title>
+
+        <para>
+          This model provides a standard way to discover and obtain the =
contents of geospatial data from the data sources and from known features=
. The query model involves the creation of Filters to sub-select the data=
 contents and expressions to extract only the relevant attributes from th=
e features of interest.
+        </para>
+
+      </sect4>
+
+      </sect3>
+
+
+
+      <sect3 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-viewComponen=
t">
+        <title>The View Component</title>
+
+        <para>
+        </para>
+
+
+        <sect4 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-display">
+          <title>The Display Model</title>
+
+          <para>
+            The display model provides a standard approach to the creati=
on of visuals through which to present the contents of a group of feature=
s. This model provides a standard approach to styling feature contents ac=
cording the complex rules which are necessary to create visually appealin=
g maps. The model also provides a rendering infrastructure for the creati=
on of images.
+          </para>
+
+        </sect4>
+
+      </sect3>
+
+
+      <sect3 id=3D"sect-conceptual-foundations-archi-subsys-controllerCo=
mponent">
+        <title>No Controller component</title>
+
+        <para>
+          There is <emphasis>no</emphasis> controller component in the G=
eotools
+          library; the component is explicitly left to be implemented by=
=20
+          library users.=20
+        </para>
+
+      </sect3>
+

+  <sect1 id=3D"sect-design-api">
+    <title>The API Layers</title>
+
     <para>
-     =20
+      The Application Programming Interface (API) to the &geot; library=20
+      consists of four seperate layers divided according to the maturity=
,=20
+      standards conformance, testing, and expected stability of the inte=
rface.
     </para>
-    <!--
-    <sect2 id=3D"">
-      <title></title>
+    =20
+    <para>=20
+      The most stable interfaces are those defined in the=20
+      <ulink url=3D"http://www.geoapi.org/" type=3D"http">GeoAPI project=
</ulink>=20
+      which aims to implement the standard java language interfaces to t=
he=20
+      major ISO and OGC geospatial standards.=20
+    </para>
+    =20
+    <para>=20
+      The &geot; library itself defines a set of stable interfaces in th=
e separate
+      <code>geotools/modules/library/api</code> module; these are interf=
aces=20
+      which have matured sufficiently to be considered stable from the=20
+      perspective of the library although the interfaces either have not=
 yet=20
+      been incorporated into GeoAPI or are not implementations of any ac=
cepted=20
+      standard and therefore do not belong in the GeoAPI interfaces.=20
+    </para>
+    =20
+    <para>=20
+      The third level of interfaces are those simply defined in the pack=
ages=20
+      themselves. These interfaces are much less stable and are expected=
 to=20
+      change between releases although all interface changes follow the =
rule =20
+      that an interface will be deprecated first for one whole release c=
ycle=20
+      prior to removal during the subsequent release cycle.
+    </para>
+    =20
+    <para>=20
+      The fourth level of interfaces are the access methods provided by =
the=20
+      libraries on which &geot; depends. The JTS library, for example, p=
rovides=20
+      a number of classes and methods which are used throughout the &geo=
t; code=20
+      base. While not technically part of the &geot; library, these inte=
rfaces=20
+      are, for practical purposes, part of the API any user program will=
 need to=20
+      use.
+    </para>
=20
+    <para>
+      Developers can use several programming interfaces through which to=
 access=20
+      the functionality of &geot;. Obviously, since the code is openly d=
istributed  =20
+      and freely accessible, users can develop their applications in any=
 way they=20
+      choose. However, there are several defined series of interfaces wh=
ich have
+      been created to allow users to develop applications which use stan=
dard=20
+      intefaces and theefore can be updated relatively easily as newer v=
ersions of=20
+      &geot; are released in the future.
+    </para>
+
+    <para>
+      While the developers using the &geot; library have the freedom to =
use this=20
+      code in any way they please, best practice dictates using the most=
 stable=20
+      interfaces possible to achieve any particular goal. This best prac=
tice=20
+      involves using the GeoAPI interfaces as extensively as possible, u=
sing the=20
+      stable &geot; interfaces where avaiable and then, only if none of =
these=20
+      provide the needed functionality, using the interfaces defined in =
each=20
+      &geot; package directly or the interfaces provided by third party=20
+      libraries. Following such a practice will lead to code which can b=
e=20
+      upgraded to newer versions of the &geot; library with the least si=
gnificant=20
+      changes.=20
+    </para>
+   =20
+    <warning>
       <para>
+        Users of &geot; should be ready to stray far from best practices=
. The=20
+        library is not yet mature enough to guarantee that even a subset=
 of=20
+        opertions can be done using only stable interfaces. During the c=
reation=20
+        of the library there have even been periods where it was impossi=
ble to=20
+        use the library without using deprecated classes.=20
       </para>
+    </warning>
=20
+<!--
+    <sect2 id=3D"sect-design-api-geoAPI">
+      <title>GeoAPI</title>
+
+      <para>
+        The GeoAPI project aims to define a set of interfaces for the=20
+        fundamental geospatial standards defined by the ISO and the OGC =
which=20
+        would allow users and implementers of the standard to code again=
st a=20
+        stable contract. Applications coded against this interface would=
 be=20
+        completely portable between independent implementations of the s=
tandards,=20
+        while implementations could seek different approaches without ha=
rming=20
+        the stability of their clients.=20
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        Unfortunately, GeoAPI is a young project, the specifications the=
mselves=20
+        are untested, and no one is sure how the interfaces will need to=
 change=20
+        as the projects seek to implement more complex semantics. While =
it will
+        hopefully eventually be possible to use &geot; by obtaining a si=
ngle=20
+        reference to one &geot; object and developing all the remaing co=
de=20
+        against the GeoAPI interfaces, that situtation will not arise in=
 the=20
+        near futre.
+      </para>
+   =20
+      <para>
+        GeoAPI is designed ... (TODO)
+      </para>

     </sect2>

+     =20
+    <para>
+      The user can generate, using the Maven 2 build tool, a skeleton=20
+      application designed to use the &geot; library and arranged=20
+      correctly to be built with maven. This system uses the 'archetype'=
 system=20
+      of the maven tool. A user must first obtain maven, create the arch=
etype,=20
+      build the archetype, and finally run the archetype. The archetype =
can then
+      be modified to create a new application.
+    </para>

+    <sect3 id=3D"sect-quick-start-archetype-getMvn">
+      <title>Get Maven 2</title>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        The Maven 2 build tool can be obtained from the Apache project. =
It must
+        be downloaded and unbundled, the Java runtime environment must b=
e=20
+        indicated by the <code>JAVA_HOME</code> environmental variable, =
and=20
+        finally the <code>mvn</code> binary can be called, possibly by h=
aving=20
+        its directory placed on the <code>PATH</code>.
+      </para>
+     =20
+    </sect3>
+   =20
+    <sect3 id=3D"sect-quick-start-archetype-create">
+      <title>Create the Archetype</title>
+     =20
+     =20
+      <para>
+        The archetype is created by the maven binary tool <code>mvn</cod=
e> based=20
+        on information obtained in a maven plugin bundle. The approach u=
sed here
+        is to first download an archetype creator plugin, next install t=
hat to=20
+        the local repository (generally .m2/repository/ under a user's h=
ome=20
+        directory), and finally to create the archetype from the plugin.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        While an archetype can be created in any directory. It is presum=
ably a=20
+        good idea to create a new, separate directory for the files such=
 as=20
+        creating a temporary directory in a users home directory. The=20
+        instructions which follow all presume a user is working within t=
hat=20
+        temporary directory.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        First, the user should download the bundle from the web. The bun=
dle is=20
+        available from the repository at Refractions Research as the=20
+        <ulink url=3D"http://lists.refractions.net/m2/org/ourgroup/geoto=
ols/base/base-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar"
+               type=3D"http">base-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar</ulink> JAR file. Thi=
s file can=20
+        be downloaded through a web browser or using a downloading tool =
like=20
+        <code>wget</code>.=20
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        Second, the file should be installed into the local repository w=
ith=20
+<literallayout>
+  mvn install:install-file -DgroupId=3Dorg.geotools.maven \=20
+                           -DartifactId=3Darchetype \=20
+                           -Dversion=3D2.4-SNAPSHOT \=20
+                           -Dpackaging=3Djar \=20
+                           -Dfile=3D./base-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
+</literallayout>
+        where the <code>2.4-SNAPSHOT</code> should be replaced by the=20
+        appropriate version number. This command will involve maven down=
loading=20
+        a number of plugins to get all the tools it needs to perform thi=
s task.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        Third, the archetype itself can be created with the command:
+        <!-- FIXME: no way to get the repository. -->
+<literallayout>
+  mvn archetype:create -Drepository=3Dlists.refractions.net/m2/ \
+                     -DarchetypeGroupId=3Dorg.geotools.maven \
+                     -DarchetypeArtifactId=3Darchetype \
+                     -DarchetypeVersion=3D2.4-SNAPSHOT \
+                     -DgroupId=3Dorg.ourgroup.geotools \
+                     -DartifactId=3Dbase
+</literallayout>
+        where, again, the <code>2.4-SNAPSHOT</code> can be replaced by t=
he appropriate=20
+        version number and where a user can choose appropriate names for=
 the=20
+        groupId and artifactId. Here again, maven will download a number=
 of=20
+        plugins to generate the artifact. This will result in the creati=
on of a=20
+        directory called <code>base/</code> in the local directory.=20
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        Fourth, the archetype must be built. The user should first chang=
e into=20
+        the <code>base/</code> directory which was created during the la=
st step=20
+        and then run the command
+<literallayout>
+  mvn install
+</literallayout>
+        which will cause maven to download more artifacts including the =
entire=20
+        set of geotools JAR files and then to build the example applicat=
ion.
+      </para>
+     =20
+      <para>
+        Finally, the archetype can be run.=20
+      </para>
+     =20
+    </sect3>
+  </sect2>
